## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic restoring + damping)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (polynomial potential)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells, preserving oscillator symmetry about equilibrium
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential, indicating broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Periodic functions of time (sin/cos of c*t) → external periodic driving forces in forced oscillators
- Negative linear damping with positive nonlinear damping (c1*v - c2*v**3 or c1*(1-x**2)*v) → limit cycle behavior
- Pure position-dependent terms with no velocity dependence → conservative (Hamiltonian) system with energy conservation
- The dominant term is almost always linear in x (c0*x with c0 < 0) representing the fundamental restoring force
- Products of time-dependent terms with x (e.g., x*cos(c*t)) → parametric excitation rather than direct forcing
